When Intercourse is Permissible After Haid/Nifas
States that when blood stops at the maximum, intercourse is permissible without ghusl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of intercourse when menstrual or postpartum bleeding stops at its maximum duration, and identify the condition (shart) that makes it permissible.

Core Idea
Intercourse is permissible once blood stops at the maximum duration, even without ghusl.

This lesson addresses a common question: when is a woman considered ritually pure after menstruation or postpartum bleeding? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the cessation of blood at the maximum period. Understanding this helps avoid unnecessary prohibition or delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is intercourse after menstruation or postpartum bleeding. The ruling is that it becomes permissible when the blood stops at the maximum duration (10 days for haid, 40 for nifas).
The text says 'حل الوطء' – it is permissible (halal).
2
Parse the condition
The condition is انقطاع الدم لأكثر الحيض والنفاس – the blood ceases at the maximum duration. This means the bleeding reached its longest possible time and then stopped.
For haid: maximum 10 days; for nifas: maximum 40 days according to Hanafis.
3
Understand the consequence
Once the condition is met, intercourse is permissible even if the woman has not performed ghusl (ritual bath). The text says 'بلا غسل' explicitly.
Ghusl is recommended before prayer, but not required for permissibility of intercourse.
4
Contrast with common misconception
Some think ghusl is a prerequisite for intercourse after haid/nifas. The Hanafi ruling clarifies that the cessation of blood is the key, not the bath.
Other schools may require ghusl; this is an intra-madhhab distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا انقطع الدّم لأكثر الحيض والنفاس، حل الوطء بلا غسل.
And when the blood stops for the maximum of menstruation and postpartum, intercourse becomes permissible without ghusl.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This is a brief ruling statement. It clarifies that the end of the menstrual or postpartum period is determined by the maximum duration (10 days for haid, 40 for nifas according to Hanafis). If the bleeding ceases at this point, the woman is considered pure, and marital relations are allowed even if she has not performed ghusl. This is based on the Quranic verse 'until they become pure' (baqarah 2:222) interpreted as the cessation of blood, not necessarily the bath. However, it is recommended to perform ghusl before prayer.

Key Terms
أكثر الحيض (akthar al-hayd): The maximum duration of menstruation, which is 10 days in the Hanafi school.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding. Maximum is 40 days according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when does intercourse become permissible for a woman whose menstrual blood stopped at the 10th day?
A) Only after she performs ghusl
B) Immediately, without ghusl
C) After she waits for one complete day
D) After she confirms by a white discharge

Key Takeaway
The cessation of blood at the maximum duration (10 days for haid, 40 for nifas) is the sole condition for the permissibility of intercourse, regardless of ghusl.

Prohibition of Intercourse and Enjoyment During Hayd and Nifas
Explanation of prohibition with intra-Hanafi dispute and kufr issue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on physical intimacy with a menstruating woman, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and apply the correct mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Intercourse and enjoyment from navel to knee are haram during hayd and nifas; the mufta bihi is the broader prohibition.

This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Idah clarifies not only that intercourse is forbidden during menstruation and post-childbirth bleeding, but also the extent of permissible physical contact. The Hanafi school has a nuanced internal difference: the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) prohibits any enjoyment from the navel to the knee, while Imam Muhammad limits the prohibition to intercourse alone. Understanding which view is operative for fatwa protects against both transgression and unnecessary hardship in marital relations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what specific physical interactions are being ruled upon: intercourse and 'enjoyment from below the navel to below the knee' during hayd and nifas. Note that the ruling is haram.
The source also mentions tawaf, but that is a digression; focus on the main issue.
2
Examine the primary proof (Quran and hadith)
Read the Quranic verses (2:222) and the hadith from Abu Dawood. Understand how each proof is used—'la taqrabuhunna' as a general prohibition, and the hadith allowing 'above the izar' to define the exception.
The hadith is the key to the dispute: it permits above the izar, implying prohibition below.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Contrast the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf (navel to knee) and Muhammad (only intercourse). Note each imam's interpretation of the same texts.
Muhammad relies on a different hadith: 'Do whatever you wish except intercourse.'
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its implication
Know that the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, so in practice one must avoid touching between navel and knee. Understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) in daily life.
The source also discusses the ruling for mustahill (one who considers it permissible) but the mufta bihi is not to declare him a disbeliever.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Take a concrete situation: a husband and wife during her menses. According to the mufta bihi, he may embrace her above the navel or below the knee, but not touch between. Understand the scope of permissible intimacy.
The prohibition on enjoyment from navel to knee includes both touching and looking with desire, per the broader view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجماع، والاستمتاع بما تحت السُّرَّة إلى تحتِ الرُّكبة. وإذا انقطع الدّم لأكثر الحيض والنفاس، حل الوطء بلا غُسل. ولقوله : ( الطَّوَافُ حَوْلَ الْبَيْتِ مِثْلُ الصَّلاةِ، إلا أنَّكُمْ تَتَكَلَّمُونَ فِيهِ، فَمَنْ تَكَلَّمَ فَلا يَتَكَلَّمَنَّ إِلا بِخَيْرِ . والمنع لشرف البيت لا لعارضية المسجد، والطهارة شرط كمال للطواف لا لصحته، (١) فيصح مع الجنابة والحيض والنفاس، وتحل به من الإحرام وعليها بدنة في الفرض، وهـو طـواف الإفاضة. وعلى المحدث شاة ما لم يعده طاهراً قبل ذبح الهدي كغيره. (وَ) يحرم بالحيض والنفاس ( الجماعُ، والاستمتاع بما تحت السُّرَّة إلى تحت الركبة)، لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا نَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ البقرة: ۲۲۲] فإن الأمر باعتزال النساء في المحيض، يمنع قربان كل بدنها، إلا أن ما وراء الإزار رخص بما رواه أبو داود عن عبد الله بن سعد قال: « سَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: مَا يَحِلُّ لِي مِنْ امْرَأَتِي وَهِيَ حَائِضٌ؟ فَقَالَ : لَكَ مَا فَوْقَ الإِزارِ » ) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبـي يـوسـف. وقال محمد: لا يحرم إلا الاستمتاع بالفرج، لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي الْمَحِيضِ [البقرة: ٢٢٢] والمحيض موضع الحيض وهو الفرج، ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( اصْنَعُوا مَا شِئْتُم إِلَّا الْجِمَاعَ» . فإن وطئها في الحيض غير مستحل له يستحب أن يتصدق بدينار أو بنصف دينار، ولا يجب ذلك، وقيل: إن كان في أول الحيض يتصدق بدينار، وإن كان في آخره فبنصف دينار، ويستغفر الله تعالى ولا يعود، وقيل: إن كان الدم أسود يتصدق بدينار، وإن كان أصفر فبنصف دينار، وكل ذلك ورد في الحديث، وإذا وطئها مستحلاً للوطء فقد جزم في « المبسوط »، و « الاختيار»، و«فتح القدير » وغيرها بكفره، وصحح في ( الخلاصة عدم كفره، لأنه إذا كان حراماً لـغـيـره لا يكفر، ولـو كـان دليله قطعياً، فلا يفتى بتكفيره لوجود وجه واحد يمنع تكفيره، وعلى المفتى أن يميل إليه. وحرمة وطء النفساء والاستمتاع بما تحت الإزار منها مصرح به، غير أني لم أر قولاً بتكفير مستحل وطئها،
And intercourse, and enjoyment from below the navel to below the knee. And when the blood stops for more than the maximum of hayd and nifas, intercourse becomes permissible without ghusl. And due to his saying: 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer, except that you speak in it, so whoever speaks should speak only good.' And the prohibition is due to the honor of the House, not because the mosque is incidental, and purification is a condition of perfection for tawaf, not for its validity, so it is valid with janaba, hayd, and nifas, and it releases one from ihram, and upon her is a camel in the obligatory (tawaf), which is tawaf al-ifada. And upon one in hadath is a sheep if he does not repeat it while pure before slaughtering the sacrifice like others. And (the author said): It is forbidden during hayd and nifas (intercourse and enjoyment from below the navel to below the knee), due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And do not approach them until they become pure' [al-Baqarah 2:222], for the command to avoid women during menstruation prohibits approaching all of her body, except that what is above the waist-wrapper is permitted by what Abu Dawood narrated from Abdullah ibn Sa'd who said: 'I asked the Messenger of Allah ﷺ: What is permissible for me from my wife when she is menstruating? He said: For you what is above the waist-wrapper.' And this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: Nothing is prohibited except enjoyment of the vagina, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'So avoid women during menstruation' [al-Baqarah 2:222], and al-mahid is the place of menstruation, which is the vagina, and due to his saying ﷺ: 'Do whatever you wish except intercourse.' And if he has intercourse with her during hayd without considering it permissible, it is recommended that he give in charity a dinar or half a dinar, and it is not obligatory, and it is said: if it is at the beginning of hayd he gives a dinar, and if at the end then half a dinar, and he asks forgiveness from Allah and does not return, and it is said: if the blood is black he gives a dinar, and if yellow then half a dinar, and all of that is reported in the hadith. And if he has intercourse considering it permissible, then it is firmly stated in al-Mabsut, al-Ikhtiyar, and Fath al-Qadir and others that he becomes a disbeliever, and it is corrected in al-Khulasa that he does not become a disbeliever, because if it is haram due to something else he does not become a disbeliever, even if its evidence is definitive, so one should not give a fatwa of his disbelief due to the existence of one aspect that prevents his disbelief, and the mufti should incline towards it. And the prohibition of intercourse with a woman in nifas and enjoyment from below the waist-wrapper is clearly stated, but I have not seen a statement regarding the disbelief of one who considers it permissible.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) on Nur al-Idah, expanding on the ruling regarding prohibited acts during menstruation (hayd) and post-childbirth bleeding (nifas). The author begins by stating the ruling: intercourse and physical enjoyment from the navel to the knee are prohibited. He then provides proof from the hadith that tawaf is like prayer, and that purification is a condition for perfection of tawaf, not validity, so it is valid even for a menstruating woman. However, if she performs the obligatory tawaf al-ifada while menstruating, she must sacrifice a camel. The author then returns to the main topic and presents the Quranic proof from al-Baqarah 2:222. He then mentions a difference of opinion among the Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that everything from the navel to the knee is prohibited, based on a hadith that permits only what is above the waist-wrapper. Muhammad holds that only intercourse is prohibited, based on another verse and the hadith 'Do whatever you wish except intercourse.' The passage also discusses the recommended charity (dinar or half) for one who has intercourse without considering it permissible, and the ruling on one who considers it permissible: some books say he becomes a disbeliever, but al-Khulasa corrects that he does not, because the prohibition is due to something external (the blood). The mufti should incline toward not declaring him a disbeliever. Finally, the author notes that the prohibition for nifas is clear, but he has not seen a ruling of disbelief for considering it permissible.

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Menstrual bleeding that occurs at regular intervals, which prohibits certain acts like prayer, fasting, and intercourse.
نفاس (nifas): Post-childbirth bleeding, which has a maximum of 40 days in the Hanafi school.
استمتاع (istimta'): Physical enjoyment or pleasure, which in this context refers to touching or intimacy with one's spouse.
إزار (izar): A waist-wrapper or lower garment, used metaphorically to distinguish between the upper and lower parts of the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, what is the extent of prohibited physical enjoyment with a menstruating woman?
A) Only intercourse is prohibited.
B) Enjoyment from the navel to the knee is prohibited.
C) Only the vagina is prohibited.
D) No physical contact is allowed at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits intercourse and any physical enjoyment from the navel to the knee during menstruation and post-childbirth bleeding, with the mufta bihi being the broader prohibition of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Intercourse After Bleeding Stops Beyond the Maximum
Ruling with proof from Quran and Hanafi principle of maximum duration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse when hayd or nifas bleeding stops beyond the maximum duration, and explain the Quranic proof and the principle that excess bleeding is istihadah.

Core Idea
Bleeding beyond 10 days (hayd) or 40 days (nifas) is istihadah; intercourse is permissible without ghusl.

In Hanafi fiqh, the cessation of menstrual or post-childbirth bleeding brings clear rulings. This lesson focuses on the simplest case: when bleeding stops after exceeding the maximum limit. You will learn the evidence from the Quran and the classification of prolonged bleeding as istihadah, which removes the prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether the bleeding stopped after the maximum duration (10 days for hayd, 40 for nifas) or within it. This lesson covers the first case.
2
State the ruling
If bleeding stops after the maximum, intercourse becomes permissible even without performing ghusl.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Analyze Surah Al-Baqarah 2:222 with the qira'ah 'yathurna' (light taa). The verse makes purity (tuhur) the limit for prohibition; once purity is achieved, the prohibition lifts.
Hanafi interprets 'yathurna' as becoming pure, which occurs after the maximum without needing ghusl.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
The maximum for hayd is 10 days. Any bleeding beyond that is istihadah. Since istihadah does not prevent intimacy, the woman is considered pure.
This principle applies whether the bleeding actually stops or not.
5
Note the recommended practice
Although intercourse is permissible without ghusl, it is recommended (mustahabb) for the husband to wait until she performs ghusl to avoid disagreement with other schools.
This shows Hanafi respect for ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا انقطع الدم لأكثر الحيض والنفاس، حلَّ الوَطْءُ بلا غُسل، لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا نَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ [البقرة: ۲۲۲] بتخفيف الطاء. جعل الطهر غاية للحرمة، وما بعد الغاية يخالف ما قبلها؛ ولأن الحيض لا مزيد له على العشرة، فيحكم بطهارتها لمضي العشرة انقطع الدم أو لم ينقطع، لأن ما زاد يكون استحاضة، كما تقدم. وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي الْمَحِيضِ لاقتضائـه قيام الحيض بهن فصار المنهي عنه وطء الحائض، وهذه ليست بحائض، ولكن يستحب له أن لا يطأها حتـى تغتسل خروجاً من الخلاف، وانقطاع النفاس لأكثر مدته مثل انقطاع الحيض لأكثره. (ولا يَحِلُّ) الوطء ( إنِ انْقَطَعَ) الحيض والنفاس عن المسلمة (لِدُونِهِ) أي: لدون الأكثر وكان انقطاعه (لِتَمَامِ عَادَتِهَا ، إلا ) بوجود أحد ثلاثة أشياء: إما أن تغتسل)، لأن زمان الغسل فيما إذا انقطع لتمام عادتها، وهي دون العشرة محسوب من الحيض، فإذا اغتسلت أخذت حكماً من أحكام الطاهرات، كقراءة القرآن، وحل الوطء من أحكامها. وقيدنا بانقطاعه لتمام عادتها لأنه لو انقطع قبل تمامها، وكان دون العشرة واغتسلت، لا يقربها حتى تنقضي عادتها، لأن العود في العادة غالب، (أو تتيمم) لعذر، وتُصلِّي) على الأصح ، فلا يحل وطؤها بمجرد التيمم حتى يتأكد بصلاة فرضاً كانت أو نفلاً، بخلاف الغسل، فإنه يحل به بمجرد الاغتسال. والثالث بينه بقوله: (أو تصير الصَّلاةُ دَيْناً في ذمتها؛ وذلك بأن تجدَ بَعْدَ الانْقِطَاع ) لتمام عادتها من الوقت الذي انقطع الدم فيه زماناً يَسَعُ الغُسل والتَّحريمةَ، فما فوقهُما ، و ( لكن ) لَم تَغْتَسِلُ) فيه ( ولم تتيمُّم حتى خرج الوقت)، فبمجرد خروجه يحل وطؤها، لترتب صلاة ذلك الوقت في ذمتها، وهو حكم من أحكام الطاهرات، واحترزنا بذلك عن إدراك جزء من آخر الوقت لا يسع الغسل مع التحريمة؛ ولذا لو طهرت قبيل الصبح بأقل من ذلك لا تجب عليها صلاة العشاء، ولا يصح صومها ذلك اليوم، كأنها أصبحت وهي حائض، ولكن عليها الإمساك تشبهاً، وتقضيه، ولا يحل وطؤها حتى تطلع الشمس إذا لم تكن اغتسلت قبل الطلوع، ولا تيممت وصلت به، وإذا انقطع قبيل طلوع الشمس بأقل من تمكنـهـا مـن الغسل والتحريمة، لا يحل وطؤها حتى يخرج وقت الظهر، كما لو انقطع في وقت الضحى، ولم تغتسل ولم تتيمم، لا يحل وطؤها حتى يخرج وقت الظهر، لتثبت صلاته في ذمتها بخروجه، لأن ما قبل الزوال وقت مهمل لا عبرة بخروجه ونبهنا بذلك احترازاً عما غلط فيه بعضهم بظنه أن المراد من قول أئمتنا، أو يمضي أدنى وقت صلاة، هو أن يمضي قدر الغسل والتحريمة بعد الانقطاع، ولــو في أول الوقت، واحترازاً عما قد يتوهم؛ من أن مضي جميع الوقت والدم منقطع شرط لحل الوطء،
And when the blood stops for more than the maximum of hayd and nifas, intercourse becomes permissible without ghusl, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And do not approach them until they become pure' [al-Baqarah 2:222] with a lightening of the taa. He made purity the limit for prohibition, and what comes after the limit contradicts what came before it; and because hayd has no increase beyond ten days, so she is judged to be purified with the passing of ten days whether the blood stops or not, because what exceeds is istihadah, as has preceded. And the saying of Allah Most High: 'So avoid women during menstruation' requires that hayd is present in them, so the prohibited thing is intercourse with a menstruating woman, and this woman is not menstruating, but it is recommended that he not have intercourse with her until she performs ghusl to exit from the difference of opinion. And the cessation of nifas for its maximum is like the cessation of hayd for its maximum. And intercourse is not permissible if hayd and nifas stop for less than the maximum, and its stopping is after the completion of her customary period, except with the existence of one of three things: either she performs ghusl, because the time of ghusl, when it stops after completion of her custom and it is less than ten, is counted from hayd, so when she performs ghusl she takes on the rulings of pure women, like reciting Quran, and permissible intercourse is among her rulings. And we restricted it to stopping after completion of her custom because if it stops before completion, and it is less than ten, and she performs ghusl, he should not approach her until her custom expires, because return of blood during the customary period is common. Or she performs tayammum due to an excuse and prays, according to the most correct, so her intercourse is not permissible by mere tayammum until it is confirmed by a prayer, whether obligatory or supererogatory, unlike ghusl, for it becomes permissible by mere washing. And the third he explained by his saying: 'Or the prayer becomes a debt in her responsibility; and that is by her finding after the cessation (after completion of her custom) in the time when the blood stopped a duration that allows the ghusl and the takbirat al-ihram and what is above them, but she did not perform ghusl and did not perform tayammum until the time exited, then by its mere exit her intercourse becomes permissible, because the prayer of that time becomes a debt on her, and that is a ruling of pure women. And we guarded by that against realizing a part of the end of the time that does not accommodate ghusl with takbirat; therefore, if she became pure just before dawn with less than that, the Isha prayer is not obligatory on her, and her fast that day is not valid, as if she woke up menstruating, but she must abstain out of emulation and make it up, and her intercourse is not permissible until sunrise if she did not perform ghusl before sunrise, nor tayammum and pray with it. And if the bleeding stops just before sunrise with less than her ability to perform ghusl and takbirat, her intercourse is not permissible until the time of Dhuhr exits, as if it stopped at the time of Duha, and she did not perform ghusl nor tayammum, her intercourse is not permissible until the time of Dhuhr exits, because her prayer becomes established in her responsibility by its exit, because what is before noon is a neglected time, and its exit is not considered. And we warned by that caution against what some have erred by thinking that the meaning of the statement of our imams, 'or the passing of the minimum time of a prayer', is that the amount of ghusl and takbirat should pass after the cessation, even if at the beginning of the time, and caution against what might be imagined, that the passing of all the time while the blood has stopped is a condition for permissibility of intercourse.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage continues from the previous lesson and explains the rulings on when intercourse becomes permissible after hayd or nifas bleeding stops. The author presents two main scenarios: First, if the bleeding stops for more than the maximum period (10 days for hayd, 40 for nifas), intercourse becomes permissible without the need for ghusl. This is based on the Quranic verse which makes purity (tuhur) the limit, and once the maximum is exceeded, the woman is considered pure even if bleeding continues, as it would be istihadah. Second, if the bleeding stops for less than the maximum but after the completion of her customary period (which is less than 10), intercourse is not permissible unless one of three conditions is met: (1) she performs ghusl; (2) she performs tayammum (if she has an excuse) and prays; (3) the prayer time ends without her having performed ghusl or tayammum, so that the prayer becomes a debt on her. The author explains the details of each condition, including the necessity of performing a prayer after tayammum to confirm purity, and the calculation of time for the third condition. He also discusses edge cases: if she becomes pure just before dawn with insufficient time for ghusl, the Isha prayer is not obligatory, and intercourse is not permissible until sunrise. If she becomes pure before dawn with enough time but she doesn't perform ghusl or tayammum, then when the Fajr time enters? Actually, the text says if she becomes pure just before sunrise with less than time for ghusl and takbir, then intercourse is not permissible until Dhuhr time exits. This is because the time before noon is a 'neglected time' (mughmal) and its exit does not establish a prayer debt. The author concludes by cautioning against misunderstandings: some think the condition is the mere passage of time sufficient for ghusl after cessation, even at the beginning of the time, but that is incorrect.

Key Terms
عادة ('adah): The customary duration of a woman's menstrual period, used to determine when she is expected to become pure.
استحاضة (istihadah): Chronic non-menstrual bleeding that is not hayd or nifas; a woman in istihadah can pray and fast but must wash for each prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman's hayd bleeding stops on the 11th day. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on intercourse?
A) It is not permissible until she performs ghusl.
B) It is permissible immediately without ghusl.
C) It is permissible only after tayammum.
D) It is not permissible because bleeding stopped before the maximum.

Key Takeaway
When hayd or nifas bleeding stops after the maximum duration, the woman is pure and intercourse is permissible without ghusl, though ghusl is recommended.

Three Conditions for Intercourse After Bleeding Stops Within the Maximum
Explains three conditions for permissibility when bleeding stops within max but after custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the three conditions that make intercourse permissible when hayd or nifas bleeding stops within the maximum but after the customary period, and explain the timing requirements for the prayer-debt condition.

Core Idea
When bleeding stops after custom but within max, intercourse requires ghusl, or tayammum with prayer, or the prayer time ending with a debt.

This lesson deals with the more nuanced case: a woman's bleeding stops after her usual habit but before the ten-day maximum. In Hanafi fiqh, she is not automatically pure; rather, three alternative conditions can make intercourse permissible. We will explore each condition and the important role of prayer times.

Guided Path
1
Recall the base scenario
Bleeding stops within the maximum (less than 10 days for hayd, less than 40 for nifas) but after completion of her customary period ('adah).
If bleeding stops before her custom ends, different rules apply (e.g., must wait for custom to expire).
2
Identify the three conditions
List the three conditions that make intercourse permissible: (1) she performs ghusl, (2) she performs tayammum (if water unavailable) and prays, (3) the time for a prayer exits while she has enough time to perform ghusl and takbir but does not, so the prayer becomes a debt on her.
Each condition independently makes her pure.
3
Understand condition 1: ghusl alone
Performing ghusl after bleeding stops during the customary period immediately makes intercourse permissible. This is because she has taken a ruling of purity.
No prayer is needed after ghusl for this ruling.
4
Understand condition 2: tayammum with prayer
If she has a valid excuse (no water), she can perform tayammum. However, tayammum alone is not sufficient; she must also perform a prayer (obligatory or supererogatory) to confirm purity.
The prayer 'locks in' the purity from tayammum.
5
Understand condition 3: prayer becomes a debt
If she has enough time to perform ghusl and say the takbirat al-ihram before the prayer time ends, but she does not, then when the time exits, the prayer becomes a debt on her. At that moment, intercourse becomes permissible because she is considered to have taken on a ruling of purity.
This applies only if she had sufficient time; if she did not, the condition is not met.

وإذا انقطع الدم لأكثر الحيض والنفاس، حلَّ الوَطْءُ بلا غُسل، لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا نَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ [البقرة: ۲۲۲] بتخفيف الطاء. جعل الطهر غاية للحرمة، وما بعد الغاية يخالف ما قبلها؛ ولأن الحيض لا مزيد له على العشرة، فيحكم بطهارتها لمضي العشرة انقطع الدم أو لم ينقطع، لأن ما زاد يكون استحاضة، كما تقدم. وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي الْمَحِيضِ لاقتضائـه قيام الحيض بهن فصار المنهي عنه وطء الحائض، وهذه ليست بحائض، ولكن يستحب له أن لا يطأها حتـى تغتسل خروجاً من الخلاف، وانقطاع النفاس لأكثر مدته مثل انقطاع الحيض لأكثره. (ولا يَحِلُّ) الوطء ( إنِ انْقَطَعَ) الحيض والنفاس عن المسلمة (لِدُونِهِ) أي: لدون الأكثر وكان انقطاعه (لِتَمَامِ عَادَتِهَا ، إلا ) بوجود أحد ثلاثة أشياء: إما أن تغتسل)، لأن زمان الغسل فيما إذا انقطع لتمام عادتها، وهي دون العشرة محسوب من الحيض، فإذا اغتسلت أخذت حكماً من أحكام الطاهرات، كقراءة القرآن، وحل الوطء من أحكامها. وقيدنا بانقطاعه لتمام عادتها لأنه لو انقطع قبل تمامها، وكان دون العشرة واغتسلت، لا يقربها حتى تنقضي عادتها، لأن العود في العادة غالب، (أو تتيمم) لعذر، وتُصلِّي) على الأصح ، فلا يحل وطؤها بمجرد التيمم حتى يتأكد بصلاة فرضاً كانت أو نفلاً، بخلاف الغسل، فإنه يحل به بمجرد الاغتسال. والثالث بينه بقوله: (أو تصير الصَّلاةُ دَيْناً في ذمتها؛ وذلك بأن تجدَ بَعْدَ الانْقِطَاع ) لتمام عادتها من الوقت الذي انقطع الدم فيه زماناً يَسَعُ الغُسل والتَّحريمةَ، فما فوقهُما ، و ( لكن ) لَم تَغْتَسِلُ) فيه ( ولم تتيمُّم حتى خرج الوقت)، فبمجرد خروجه يحل وطؤها، لترتب صلاة ذلك الوقت في ذمتها، وهو حكم من أحكام الطاهرات، واحترزنا بذلك عن إدراك جزء من آخر الوقت لا يسع الغسل مع التحريمة؛ ولذا لو طهرت قبيل الصبح بأقل من ذلك لا تجب عليها صلاة العشاء، ولا يصح صومها ذلك اليوم، كأنها أصبحت وهي حائض، ولكن عليها الإمساك تشبهاً، وتقضيه، ولا يحل وطؤها حتى تطلع الشمس إذا لم تكن اغتسلت قبل الطلوع، ولا تيممت وصلت به، وإذا انقطع قبيل طلوع الشمس بأقل من تمكنـهـا مـن الغسل والتحريمة، لا يحل وطؤها حتى يخرج وقت الظهر، كما لو انقطع في وقت الضحى، ولم تغتسل ولم تتيمم، لا يحل وطؤها حتى يخرج وقت الظهر، لتثبت صلاته في ذمتها بخروجه، لأن ما قبل الزوال وقت مهمل لا عبرة بخروجه ونبهنا بذلك احترازاً عما غلط فيه بعضهم بظنه أن المراد من قول أئمتنا، أو يمضي أدنى وقت صلاة، هو أن يمضي قدر الغسل والتحريمة بعد الانقطاع، ولــو في أول الوقت، واحترازاً عما قد يتوهم؛ من أن مضي جميع الوقت والدم منقطع شرط لحل الوطء،
And when the blood stops for more than the maximum of hayd and nifas, intercourse becomes permissible without ghusl, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And do not approach them until they become pure' [al-Baqarah 2:222] with a lightening of the taa. He made purity the limit for prohibition, and what comes after the limit contradicts what came before it; and because hayd has no increase beyond ten days, so she is judged to be purified with the passing of ten days whether the blood stops or not, because what exceeds is istihadah, as has preceded. And the saying of Allah Most High: 'So avoid women during menstruation' requires that hayd is present in them, so the prohibited thing is intercourse with a menstruating woman, and this woman is not menstruating, but it is recommended that he not have intercourse with her until she performs ghusl to exit from the difference of opinion. And the cessation of nifas for its maximum is like the cessation of hayd for its maximum. And intercourse is not permissible if hayd and nifas stop for less than the maximum, and its stopping is after the completion of her customary period, except with the existence of one of three things: either she performs ghusl, because the time of ghusl, when it stops after completion of her custom and it is less than ten, is counted from hayd, so when she performs ghusl she takes on the rulings of pure women, like reciting Quran, and permissible intercourse is among her rulings. And we restricted it to stopping after completion of her custom because if it stops before completion, and it is less than ten, and she performs ghusl, he should not approach her until her custom expires, because return of blood during the customary period is common. Or she performs tayammum due to an excuse and prays, according to the most correct, so her intercourse is not permissible by mere tayammum until it is confirmed by a prayer, whether obligatory or supererogatory, unlike ghusl, for it becomes permissible by mere washing. And the third he explained by his saying: 'Or the prayer becomes a debt in her responsibility; and that is by her finding after the cessation (after completion of her custom) in the time when the blood stopped a duration that allows the ghusl and the takbirat al-ihram and what is above them, but she did not perform ghusl and did not perform tayammum until the time exited, then by its mere exit her intercourse becomes permissible, because the prayer of that time becomes a debt on her, and that is a ruling of pure women. And we guarded by that against realizing a part of the end of the time that does not accommodate ghusl with takbirat; therefore, if she became pure just before dawn with less than that, the Isha prayer is not obligatory on her, and her fast that day is not valid, as if she woke up menstruating, but she must abstain out of emulation and make it up, and her intercourse is not permissible until sunrise if she did not perform ghusl before sunrise, nor tayammum and pray with it. And if the bleeding stops just before sunrise with less than her ability to perform ghusl and takbirat, her intercourse is not permissible until the time of Dhuhr exits, as if it stopped at the time of Duha, and she did not perform ghusl nor tayammum, her intercourse is not permissible until the time of Dhuhr exits, because her prayer becomes established in her responsibility by its exit, because what is before noon is a neglected time, and its exit is not considered. And we warned by that caution against what some have erred by thinking that the meaning of the statement of our imams, 'or the passing of the minimum time of a prayer', is that the amount of ghusl and takbirat should pass after the cessation, even if at the beginning of the time, and caution against what might be imagined, that the passing of all the time while the blood has stopped is a condition for permissibility of intercourse.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage continues from the previous lesson and explains the rulings on when intercourse becomes permissible after hayd or nifas bleeding stops. The author presents two main scenarios: First, if the bleeding stops for more than the maximum period (10 days for hayd, 40 for nifas), intercourse becomes permissible without the need for ghusl. This is based on the Quranic verse which makes purity (tuhur) the limit, and once the maximum is exceeded, the woman is considered pure even if bleeding continues, as it would be istihadah. Second, if the bleeding stops for less than the maximum but after the completion of her customary period (which is less than 10), intercourse is not permissible unless one of three conditions is met: (1) she performs ghusl; (2) she performs tayammum (if she has an excuse) and prays; (3) the prayer time ends without her having performed ghusl or tayammum, so that the prayer becomes a debt on her. The author explains the details of each condition, including the necessity of performing a prayer after tayammum to confirm purity, and the calculation of time for the third condition. He also discusses edge cases: if she becomes pure just before dawn with insufficient time for ghusl, the Isha prayer is not obligatory, and intercourse is not permissible until sunrise. If she becomes pure before dawn with enough time but she doesn't perform ghusl or tayammum, then when the Fajr time enters? Actually, the text says if she becomes pure just before sunrise with less than time for ghusl and takbir, then intercourse is not permissible until Dhuhr time exits. This is because the time before noon is a 'neglected time' (mughmal) and its exit does not establish a prayer debt. The author concludes by cautioning against misunderstandings: some think the condition is the mere passage of time sufficient for ghusl after cessation, even at the beginning of the time, but that is incorrect.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) of the prayer, used as a minimum measure for the time sufficient to perform ghusl and start a prayer.
عادة ('adah): The customary duration of a woman's menstrual period.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman with a 5-day custom bleeds for 7 days and then stops. She has a valid excuse and performs tayammum but does not pray. According to the passage, is intercourse permissible?
A) Yes, because tayammum purifies.
B) No, because tayammum must be confirmed by a prayer.
C) Yes, because bleeding stopped after her custom.
D) No, because she must perform ghusl.

Key Takeaway
When bleeding stops after the customary period but within the maximum, intercourse requires either ghusl, or tayammum with prayer, or the exit of a prayer time after she had sufficient opportunity to purify.

Conditions for Intercourse After Menstrual Bleeding Stops Before Ten Days
Expansion of a matn ruling with proof and detailed conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi conditions for permissible intercourse after menstruation stops before ten days, identify the Quranic proof, and explain why mafhum al-shart is not accepted as a proof.

Core Idea
Intercourse after menstruation before ten days requires ghusl, tayammum with prayer, or the lapse of a full prayer time.

This passage from Nur al-Idah explains a nuanced Hanafi ruling: when a woman's menstrual bleeding stops before the maximum ten days but at completion of her habit, intercourse is not automatically permissible. The school stipulates three alternative conditions that must be met. The author also addresses objections based on a variant Quranic reading and the implication of condition (mafhum al-shart), providing the Hanafi rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Determine the act (intercourse after bleeding stops before ten days) and the default ruling: it is prohibited during bleeding, and after cessation it becomes permissible only if one of three conditions is met. The overall hukm is mubah but contingent.
The default permissibility is not immediate; conditions must be verified.
2
List the three alternative conditions
From the text, note the three conditions: (1) she performs ghusl, (2) she performs tayammum due to an excuse and then prays any prayer, (3) a full prayer time passes without her doing ghusl or tayammum, making prayer a debt upon her.
These are alternative, not cumulative.
3
Understand the timing requirements
For the third condition, she must have had sufficient time after cessation to perform ghusl and the opening takbir (tahrimah) within a prayer time, but she did not. If the time is insufficient, the ruling differs (e.g., if only a short time remains before fajr, she must wait for zuhr to pass).
The key is whether she had the opportunity to purify but did not use it.
4
Analyze the Quranic proof and variant readings
The author cites Quran 2:222, which has two readings: one with tashdid (hata yat taharna) implying ghusl is required, and one with takhfif (hata yat hurna) implying mere cessation. The Hanafi school reconciles them: cessation suffices for maximum ten days, but within that period, one of the three conditions is needed.
The dalil is zanni al-dalala due to the variant readings.
5
Evaluate the objection regarding mafhum al-shart
Some argue that the verse 'when they have purified themselves' (mafhum al-shart) prohibits intercourse before ghusl. The Hanafi response is that mafhum al-shart is not a valid proof (hujja) in Hanafi usul. Therefore, the ruling is derived from the combination of readings, not from the conditional implication alone.
This is a fundamental usul difference with schools that accept mafhum al-shart.

الحيض لا مزيد له على العشرة، فيحكم بطهارتها لمضي العشرة انقطع الدم أو لم ينقطع، لأن ما زاد يكون استحاضة، كما تقدم. وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي الْمَحِيضِ لاقتضائـه قيام الحيض بهن فصار المنهي عنه وطء الحائض، وهذه ليست بحائض، ولكن يستحب له أن لا يطأها حتـى تغتسل خروجاً من الخلاف، وانقطاع النفاس لأكثر مدته مثل انقطاع الحيض لأكثره. (ولا يَحِلُّ) الوطء ( إنِ انْقَطَعَ) الحيض والنفاس عن المسلمة (لِدُونِهِ) أي: لدون الأكثر وكان انقطاعه (لِتَمَامِ عَادَتِهَا ، إلا ) بوجود أحد ثلاثة أشياء: إما أن تغتسل)، لأن زمان الغسل فيما إذا انقطع لتمام عادتها، وهي دون العشرة محسوب من الحيض، فإذا اغتسلت أخذت حكماً من أحكام الطاهرات، كقراءة القرآن، وحل الوطء من أحكامها. وقيدنا بانقطاعه لتمام عادتها لأنه لو انقطع قبل تمامها، وكان دون العشرة واغتسلت، لا يقربها حتى تنقضي عادتها، لأن العود في العادة غالب، (أو تتيمم) لعذر، وتُصلِّي) على الأصح ، فلا يحل وطؤها بمجرد التيمم حتى يتأكد بصلاة فرضاً كانت أو نفلاً، بخلاف الغسل، فإنه يحل به بمجرد الاغتسال. والثالث بينه بقوله: (أو تصير الصَّلاةُ دَيْناً في ذمتها؛ وذلك بأن تجدَ بَعْدَ الانْقِطَاع ) لتمام عادتها من الوقت الذي انقطع الدم فيه زماناً يَسَعُ الغُسل والتَّحريمةَ، فما فوقهُما ، و ( لكن ) لَم تَغْتَسِلُ) فيه ( ولم تتيمُّم حتى خرج الوقت)، فبمجرد خروجه يحل وطؤها، لترتب صلاة ذلك الوقت في ذمتها، وهو حكم من أحكام الطاهرات، واحترزنا بذلك عن إدراك جزء من آخر الوقت لا يسع الغسل مع التحريمة؛ ولذا لو طهرت قبيل الصبح بأقل من ذلك لا تجب عليها صلاة العشاء، ولا يصح صومها ذلك اليوم، كأنها أصبحت وهي حائض، ولكن عليها الإمساك تشبهاً، وتقضيه، ولا يحل وطؤها حتى تطلع الشمس إذا لم تكن اغتسلت قبل الطلوع، ولا تيممت وصلت به، وإذا انقطع قبيل طلوع الشمس بأقل من تمكنـهـا مـن الغسل والتحريمة، لا يحل وطؤها حتى يخرج وقت الظهر، كما لو انقطع في وقت الضحى، ولم تغتسل ولم تتيمم، لا يحل وطؤها حتى يخرج وقت الظهر، لتثبت صلاته في ذمتها بخروجه، لأن ما قبل الزوال وقت مهمل لا عبرة بخروجه ونبهنا بذلك احترازاً عما غلط فيه بعضهم بظنه أن المراد من قول أئمتنا، أو يمضي أدنى وقت صلاة، هو أن يمضي قدر الغسل والتحريمة بعد الانقطاع، ولــو في أول الوقت، واحترازاً عما قد يتوهم؛ من أن مضي جميع الوقت والدم منقطع شرط لحل الوطء،
وقيدنا بالمسلمة، لأن الكتابية يحل وطؤها بنفس الانقطاع لتمام عادتها قبل العشرة، لأنه لا ينتظر في حقها أمارة زائدة؛ لعدم خطابها بالفروع، ولا يتغير الحكم بإسلامها بعده، فحكمنا بخروجها من الحيض قبله، وقيدنا بانقطاعه لتمام عادتها، لأنه لو انقطع لدونها وقد تجاوز ثلاثة أيام لا يقربها، وإن اغتسلت، حتى تمضي عادتها، لأن العود في العادة غالب، ولكن تصوم وتصلي احتياطاً، ويجب عليها تأخير الغسل إلى قبيل آخر الوقت المستحب، وأما إذا انقطع لتمام عادتها فيستحب التأخير إليه، حتى إذا انقطع في أول وقت العشاء، تؤخر الغسل إلى وقت يمكنها أن تغتسل فيه وتصلي قبل انقضاء نصف الليل، لأن ما بعده مكروه، وإن انقطع لدون عادتها كذلك، وجب تأخيرها إلى آخــر الليل، بحيث يبقى منه ما يسع الغسل والصلاة قبل الفجر احتياطاً في أمر الصلاة، ولا يقربها زوجها حتى تمضي عادتها كما ذكرناه. تنبيه: افترق الحكم بحل الوطء فيما إذا انقطع لأكثر مدته من غير شرط زائد عن الحكم بحله فيما إذا انقطع لدون الأكثر لتمام العادة، إلا بأحد الأمور الثلاثة، لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يظهرن [البقرة : ۲۲۲] قرئ بالتشديد والتخفيف، فمقتضى قراءة التخفيف: انتهاء الحرمـة الـعـارضـة على الحل بالانقطاع مطلقاً، أي: سواء كان العشرة أو لدونها، وإذا انتهت الحرمـة حــل الــوطء بالضرورة، ومقتضى قراءة التشديد عدم انتهاء الحرمة عند الانقطاع مطلقاً حتى تغتسل، فالتوفيق بينهما بما قلناه، لأن بانقطاعه لأكثر مدته جعلها الشرع طاهرة، بدليل وجوب الصلاة عليها جزماً، فلو توقف حل وطئها على غسل لكانت حائضاً حكماً مع عدم زيادته عليها قطعاً، بخلاف انقطاعه لتمام العادة فيما دونه، لأن الشرع لم يقطع بالطهر، بل جوزه بعده، ولهذا لو زاد عليها ولم يتجاوز العشرة كان الكل حيضاً فإن قيل : حمل قراءة التشديد على الانقطاع لتمـام الـعـادة يقتضي حرمة الوطء قبل الغسل فحله قبله بخروج الوقت معارضة للنص بالتعليل، وأنه لا يجوز. وأجـيـب بـأن قراءة التشديد خص منها صورة الانقطاع لتمام العشرة بقراءة التخفيف، فجاز أن يخص ثانياً بالتعليل، فإن قيل: ترتيب الإتيان على التطهر في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا تَطَهَّرْنَ فَأْتُوهُنَ ﴾ [البقة : ۲۲۲] يقتضي عدم جوازه ،قبله، قلنا: ذلك بمفهوم الشرط، وهو ليس حجة عندنا كما تقرر في الأصول.
And it is not permissible if it (bleeding) stops before its maximum but after completion of her habit (of menstruation) except that she performs ghusl, or performs tayammum and prays, or prayer becomes a debt in her responsibility; that is, she finds after the stoppage from the time the bleeding stopped – a time sufficient for ghusl and the opening takbir, and what is above them, and she did not perform ghusl and did not perform tayammum until the time exited. Menstruation has no increase beyond ten days, so it is ruled that she is pure after ten days pass, whether the bleeding stops or not, because what is beyond is istihadah (irregular bleeding), as has preceded. And His (Allah's) statement: « So keep away from women during menstruation » because it necessitates the existence of menstruation in them, so the prohibited thing becomes intercourse with a menstruating woman, and this (one who stopped) is not menstruating, but it is recommended that he not have intercourse with her until she performs ghusl to exit from the difference (of opinion). And the stoppage of postpartum bleeding for its maximum duration is like the stoppage of menstruation for its maximum. (And it is not permissible) intercourse (if) menstruation or postpartum bleeding stops (for a Muslim woman) (before its maximum) and its stoppage (was at the completion of her habit) except with the existence of one of three things: either she performs ghusl, because the time of ghusl when it stops at completion of her habit, and it (the stoppage) is before ten days, is counted from menstruation, so when she performs ghusl she takes a ruling from the rulings of pure women, like reciting Quran, and permissibility of intercourse is from its rulings. And we restricted (the ruling) to stoppage at completion of her habit because if it stops before its completion, and it was before ten days and she performs ghusl, he may not approach her until her habit passes, because return (of bleeding) with the habit is dominant. (Or she performs tayammum) due to an excuse, and prays according to the most correct, so intercourse is not permissible for him merely by tayammum until it is confirmed by a prayer, obligatory or voluntary, unlike ghusl, for it becomes permissible by the mere act of ghusl. And the third (condition) is explained by his saying: (or prayer becomes a debt in her responsibility; that is, she finds after the stoppage) at completion of her habit, from the time the bleeding stopped, a time sufficient for ghusl and the opening takbir, and what is above them, and (but) she did not perform ghusl and did not perform tayammum until the time exited. So by its mere exit, intercourse becomes permissible for her, due to the obligation of that time's prayer in her responsibility, and it is a ruling from the rulings of pure women. And we guarded by that against realizing a part of the end of the time that does not accommodate ghusl with the opening takbir; hence if she becomes pure shortly before dawn with less than that, the isha prayer is not obligatory upon her, and her fast on that day is not valid, as if she became in the morning while menstruating, but she must refrain (from food) imitation (of fasting) and make it up, and intercourse is not permissible for her until the sun rises if she did not perform ghusl before sunrise, nor perform tayammum and pray with it. And if it stops shortly before sunrise with less than her ability to perform ghusl and the opening takbir, intercourse does not become permissible for her until the time of zuhr exits, just as if it stopped in forenoon time, and she did not perform ghusl nor tayammum, intercourse does not become permissible for her until the time of zuhr exits, in order to establish her prayer (of zuhr) in her responsibility by its exit, because what is before noon is a neglected time, its exit is not considered. And we alerted by that as a precaution against what some erred in, thinking that the intent of the saying of our imams 'or the minimum time for a prayer passes' is that the amount of ghusl and the opening takbir passes after stoppage, even if at the beginning of the time, and as a precaution against what may be imagined, that the passing of the entire time while blood is stopped is a condition for the permissibility of intercourse. And we restricted (the ruling) to the Muslim woman, because for the Kitabiyya (scriptuary woman), intercourse becomes permissible by the mere stoppage at completion of her habit before ten days, because no additional sign is awaited in her case, due to her not being addressed with the subsidiary rulings, and her ruling does not change by her Islam after that, so we ruled her exiting from menstruation before it (the 10 days). And we restricted (the ruling) to stoppage at completion of her habit, because if it stops before her habit and it has exceeded three days, he may not approach her, even if she performs ghusl, until her habit passes, because return (of bleeding) with the habit is dominant, but she fasts and prays as a precaution, and it is obligatory upon her to delay ghusl until near the end of the recommended time. As for when it stops at completion of her habit, it is recommended to delay it to that time, so that if it stops at the beginning of the time of isha, she delays ghusl to a time when she can perform ghusl and pray before half the night passes, because what is after that is disliked. And if it stops before her habit similarly, it is obligatory for her to delay to the end of the night, such that enough remains for ghusl and prayer before dawn as a precaution regarding prayer, and her husband may not approach her until her habit passes as we mentioned. Note: The ruling on the permissibility of intercourse when it stops for its maximum duration without an additional condition differs from the ruling on its permissibility when it stops before the maximum at completion of the habit except with one of three things, because the statement of Allah « And do not approach them until they become pure » (Quran 2:222) is recited with tashdid (shaddah) and takhfif (without shaddah). So the implication of the takhfif reading: the end of the prohibition that overrides permissibility by cessation absolutely, i.e., whether at ten days or before it, and when the prohibition ends, intercourse becomes permissible by necessity. And the implication of the tashdid reading: the prohibition does not end at cessation absolutely until she performs ghusl. So reconciliation between them is what we have said, because by its stopping at its maximum duration, the Law (shar') considers her pure, evidenced by the obligation of prayer upon her definitively, so if her intercourse were to depend on ghusl, she would be a menstruant in ruling despite no increase (of bleeding) upon her definitively. Unlike the case of it stopping at completion of the habit within that (maximum), because the Law does not decide purity, but rather allows it after that, and therefore if it increases upon her without exceeding ten days, all of it is menstruation. If it is said: applying the tashdid reading to stoppage at completion of the habit implies prohibition of intercourse before ghusl, so permitting it before that (ghusl) by the exit of time is opposing the text by reasoning, and that is not permissible. And it is answered that the tashdid reading is exempted from it the case of stoppage at completion of ten days by the takhfif reading, so it is allowed to exempt (from it) a second time by reasoning. If it is said: the ordering of coming (to women) after purification in His statement « So when they have purified themselves, go in unto them » (Quran 2:222) implies that it is not permissible before that, we say: that is by the implication of condition (mafhum al-shart), and it is not a proof according to us, as established in usul.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the conditions under which a Muslim man may have intercourse with his wife when her menstrual (hayd) or postpartum (nifas) bleeding stops before reaching the maximum duration (10 days for hayd, 40 days for nifas), but after her usual habit ('adah). The author, following the Hanafi school, explains that if the bleeding stops at the completion of her habit (which is less than the maximum), intercourse is not automatically permissible. There are three conditions that allow it: (1) she performs ghusl (ritual bath); (2) she performs tayammum (dry ablution) due to a legitimate excuse and then prays; or (3) a full prayer time passes without her performing ghusl or tayammum, making prayer a debt upon her. The author distinguishes between these conditions and explains their rationale. For instance, ghusl alone suffices because the time for ghusl is considered part of hayd, so after ghusl she takes rulings of purity. Tayammum requires prayer to confirm the ruling. The third condition relies on the fact that obligation of prayer is a sign of purity. The passage also discusses special cases: the ruling for a non-Muslim (kitabiyya) wife, where intercourse becomes permissible immediately upon cessation at her habit because she is not obligated to pray. Additionally, it covers scenarios where the bleeding stops before the habit (less than the usual duration) — in that case, caution dictates waiting until the full habit passes, though she must pray and fast during the intervening period. The author then provides a deeper analysis using the two variant readings of Quran 2:222 (with and without shaddah), reconciling them through the Hanafi principle that mafhum al-shart (implication of condition) is not a valid proof. This reconciliation explains why the Hanafi school requires one of these three conditions rather than immediate permissibility or requiring ghusl absolutely.

Key Terms
عادتها ('adataha): The woman's usual habit (duration and pattern) of menstruation, which may be less than the maximum of ten days.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir of the prayer (Allahu akbar), used here to measure the minimum time needed to begin a prayer.
استحاضة (istihadah): Irregular bleeding outside the normal menstrual period; it is considered a valid excuse (udhr) but does not prevent prayer or fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what makes intercourse permissible after menstruation stops at completion of habit but before ten days, if she does not perform ghusl or tayammum?
A) The mere cessation of bleeding
B) The passage of a full prayer time without her performing ghusl or tayammum
C) Her husband's permission
D) The passage of three days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling requires one of three conditions for intercourse after menstruation stops before ten days: ghusl, tayammum with prayer, or lapse of a full prayer time.

Menstruating Woman Must Make Up Missed Fasts but Not Missed Prayers
Ruling with proof via hadith of Aisha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada' of prayers and fasts for a menstruating or postpartum woman and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman must make up missed fasts but not prayers, as established by the explicit hadith.

This lesson addresses a common question: if a woman misses prayers and fasts due to menstruation or postpartum bleeding, what must she compensate? The ruling is clear and based on a direct hadith from 'Aisha. Understanding this distinction is essential for every Muslim woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The text states that a menstruating and postpartum woman must make up (taqdi) the fast, not the prayer. Recognize the hukm: making up fasts is wajib; prayers are waived entirely.
The ruling applies to both hayd and nifas.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is a hadith narrated by Mu'adha bint 'Abdillah, who asked 'Aisha about this distinction. 'Aisha responded that they (the women during the Prophet's time) were commanded to make up fasts but not prayers.
This is a sound hadith (ahad) but sufficient evidence for the ruling.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith explicitly mentions the command (nu'meru) to make up fasts and the absence of command to make up prayers. This explicit distinction is taken as binding by the Hanafi school.
The command indicates obligation (wujub) for fasts; the lack of command indicates the prayer is completely waived.
4
Note the Wisdom Behind the Ruling
Prayer is repeated daily and requires ritual purity; making up every missed prayer would be extremely burdensome. Fasts, however, occur only once a year and can be made up without excessive difficulty.
This wisdom is derived from the hadith and the principles of the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وتقضي الحائض والنفساءُ الصَّومَ دونَ الصَّلاةِ) لحديث معاذة بنت عبد الله العدوي، قالت: « سَأَلْتُ عَائِشَةَ ، فَقُلْتُ: مَا بَالُ الْحَائِضِ تَقْضِي الصَّوْمَ وَلَا تَقْضِي الصَّلاةَ؟ فَقَالَتْ: أَحَرُورِيَّةٌ أَنْتِ؟ قُلْتُ: لَسْتُ بِحَرُورِيَّةٍ، وَلَكِنِّي أَسْأَلُ قَالَتْ: كَانَ يُصِيبُنَا ذَلِكَ، فَنُؤْمَرُ بِقَضَاءِ الصَّوْمِ وَلَا نُؤْمَرُ بِقَضَاءِ
(And the menstruating and postpartum woman must make up the fast, not the prayer) due to the hadith of Mu'adha bint 'Abdillah al-'Adawiyya: she said, 'I asked 'Aisha and said: Why does the menstruating woman make up the fast but not make up the prayer? She said: Are you a Haruriyya (a Kharijite)? I said: I am not a Haruriyya, but I am asking. She said: That used to happen to us, so we were commanded to make up the fast but were not commanded to make up the prayer.'
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: a woman who experiences menstruation (hayd) or postpartum bleeding (nifas) is excused from performing prayer during those days, and she does not have to make up those missed prayers after she becomes pure. However, she is required to make up the fasts (siyam) of Ramadan that she missed due to hayd or nifas. The proof is a well-known hadith from 'Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her). The hadith is quoted partially; the full version includes the explanation that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded them to make up the fasts but not the prayers. This ruling is based on the principle that prayer is an act requiring physical purity (taharah) which is lacking during menses, and it is repeated daily, so making up all missed prayers would be excessively burdensome. Fasts, however, are few in number (only one month a year) and are compensated without excessive difficulty. The Hanafi school follows this position unanimously.

Key Terms
تقضي (taqdi): She makes up or compensates an obligatory act (fast) after the excuse is removed.
حائض (ha'id): A woman experiencing menstrual bleeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what must a menstruating woman make up?
A) Both missed prayers and missed fasts
B) Only missed prayers
C) Only missed fasts
D) Neither, as they are all waived

Key Takeaway
A menstruating or postpartum woman must make up missed fasts but not prayers, as per the explicit hadith and consensus of the Hanafi school.

Reconciling the Two Readings on Intercourse After Menstruation
Reconciliation of conflicting qira'at on intercourse after menstruation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school reconciles the two qira'at of Surah al-Baqarah 2:222 and apply the ruling on when intercourse becomes permissible after menstruation.

Core Idea
The two readings are reconciled by distinguishing cessation after the maximum duration from cessation at the habit's end.

This lesson examines a nuanced Hanafi ruling derived from the two authenticated readings (qira'at) of Quran 2:222. The verse prohibits approaching menstruating women 'until they are pure' – but the word 'yat'hurna' has been recited with and without a shaddah, implying different conditions for purity. The Hanafi school harmonizes these readings through a careful textual and rational analysis, resulting in a detailed ruling that depends on the duration of bleeding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Qira'at
Note that the same verse has been recited in two ways: with tashdid (yat'hurna – emphasizes purification) and takhfif (yat'hurna – without emphasis). Each reading suggests a different condition for permissibility of intercourse.
These are both authentic mutawatir readings.
2
Understand the Apparent Conflict
The takhfif reading implies that the prohibition ends with the mere cessation of bleeding (any duration). The tashdid reading implies that the prohibition continues until ghusl. This seems contradictory.
Some schools may prefer one reading over the other; Hanafis reconcile both.
3
Apply the Hanafi Principle of Jam' (Reconciliation)
Hanafis reconcile by distinguishing two scenarios: (1) bleeding stops after the maximum duration (ten days), and (2) bleeding stops at the completion of her habitual cycle (within ten days). In scenario 1, the Law considers her pure (e.g., prayer becomes obligatory), so intercourse is permissible immediately without ghusl. In scenario 2, the Law does not definitively rule purity, so intercourse is not permissible until after ghusl or until the habit completes.
The reasoning is supported by the fact that after the maximum, she is legally pure for prayer.
4
Address the Objections
The text presents two objections: (a) applying the tashdid reading to the habit scenario would forbid intercourse before ghusl, so allowing it by reasoning contradicts the text; (b) the verse 'when they have purified themselves' (conditional) implies intercourse only after ghusl. The Hanafi response: (a) the tashdid reading is already excepted for the ten-day case by the takhfif reading, so it can be excepted again by reasoning; (b) the conditional implication is not a valid proof in Hanafi usul.
These responses rely on Hanafi usul principles (acceptance of qiyas, rejection of mafhum al-shart).
5
Summarize the Operative Ruling
Thus, the Hanafi mufta bihi position: if bleeding stops after ten days, intercourse is permissible without ghusl. If bleeding stops at the completion of her habit (less than ten days) without exceeding the habit, it is permissible after she performs ghusl or after the time of a full prayer passes. See the three exceptions mentioned in the text.
The three exceptions are not detailed here but are part of the broader Hanafi fiqh on hayd.

تنبيه: افترق الحكم بحل الوطء فيما إذا انقطع لأكثر مدته من غير شرط زائد عن الحكم بحله فيما إذا انقطع لدون الأكثر لتمام العادة، إلا بأحد الأمور الثلاثة، لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٢٢] قرئ بالتشديد والتخفيف، فمقتضى قراءة التخفيف: انتهاء الحرمة العارضة على الحل بالانقطاع مطلقاً، أي: سواء كان العشرة أو لدونها، وإذا انتهت الحرمة حل الوطء بالضرورة، ومقتضى قراءة التشديد عدم انتهاء الحرمة عند الانقطاع مطلقاً حتى تغتسل، فالتوفيق بينهما بما قلناه، لأن بانقطاعه لأكثر مدته جعلها الشرع طاهرة، بدليل وجوب الصلاة عليها جزماً، فلو توقف حل وطئها على غسل لكانت حائضاً حكماً مع عدم زيادته عليها قطعاً، بخلاف انقطاعه لتمام العادة فيما دونه، لأن الشرع لم يقطع بالطهر، بل جوزه بعده، ولهذا لو زاد عليها ولم يتجاوز العشرة كان الكل حيضاً فإن قيل : حمل قراءة التشديد على الانقطاع لتمام العادة يقتضي حرمة الوطء قبل الغسل فحله قبله بخروج الوقت معارضة للنص بالتعليل، وأنه لا يجوز. وأجيب بأن قراءة التشديد خص منها صورة الانقطاع لتمام العشرة بقراءة التخفيف، فجاز أن يخص ثانياً بالتعليل، فإن قيل: ترتيب الإتيان على التطهر في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا تَطَهَّرْنَ فَأْتُوهُنَّ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٢٢] يقتضي عدم جوازه قبله، قلنا: ذلك بمفهوم الشرط، وهو ليس حجة عندنا كما تقرر في الأصول.
Note: The ruling on the permissibility of intercourse differs: when bleeding stops after its maximum duration, it is permissible without any additional condition, unlike when it stops for less than the maximum but at the completion of her habitual period, except in one of three ways. Because Allah's statement: 'And do not approach them until they are pure' [2:222] has been recited with tashdid (shaddah on 'ta') and takhif (without shaddah). The implication of the takhif reading is that the temporary prohibition expires with the cessation of bleeding absolutely, whether after ten days or less. And when the prohibition ends, intercourse becomes permissible by necessity. The implication of the tashdid reading is that the prohibition does not end absolutely with the cessation until she performs ghusl. The reconciliation between them is what we have stated: because when it stops after its maximum duration, the Law considers her pure, evidenced by the obligation of prayer upon her definitely. So if the permissibility of intercourse were conditional upon ghusl, she would be considered a menstruating woman by legal ruling even though there is definitely no increase beyond the maximum. This is unlike when it stops at the completion of her habit within less than ten days, because the Law does not definitively rule purity, but rather allows it afterwards. Hence, if it resumes and does not exceed ten days, all of it is menstruation. If it is said: Applying the tashdid reading to stopping at the completion of the habit implies prohibition of intercourse before ghusl, so allowing it before ghusl upon expiry of time is a contradiction of the text by reasoning, and that is impermissible. The answer: The tashdid reading was excepted from the case of stopping at the completion of ten days by the takhif reading, so it is possible to except it a second time by reasoning. If it is said: The ordering of approaching after purification in Allah's statement: 'And when they have purified themselves, approach them' [2:222] implies its impermissibility before then. We say: That is by way of the implication of the condition, which is not a proof according to us, as established in Usul.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a legal elaboration (ta'liq) on the ruling regarding when intercourse becomes permissible after menstrual bleeding stops. The author reconciles the two well-known qira'at (readings) of the Quranic verse (2:222). According to the takhif reading (without shaddah), the prohibition ends immediately upon the cessation of bleeding, regardless of its duration. According to the tashdid reading (with shaddah), the prohibition continues until ghusl. The Hanafi school reconciles these by distinguishing between bleeding that stops after its maximum (ten days) and bleeding that stops before that but at the completion of her habitual cycle. In the first case, since the Law considers her pure for prayer, intercourse is permissible without ghusl, because requiring ghusl would treat her as still menstruating, which is contradictory. In the second case, it is not permissible until the habit passes, because the Law does not definitively declare purity. The author then addresses an objection: if the tashdid reading is applied to the case of stopping at the habit, it would prohibit intercourse before ghusl, so allowing it upon expiry of time would be a contradiction. The response is that the tashdid reading is already excepted in the case of ten days by the takhif reading, so it can be excepted again by reasoning (ta'lil). Another objection: the verse 'when they have purified themselves' implies intercourse only after ghusl. The Hanafi response: this is a conditional implication (mafhum al-shart), which is not a valid proof in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تشديد (tashdīd): Reading with a shaddah on the letter ta in the word 'yat'hurna', indicating emphasis and implying continuity of prohibition until ghusl.
تخفيف (takhfīf): Reading without shaddah, implying that the prohibition ends with the cessation of bleeding itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi reconciliation of the two qira'at, when does intercourse become permissible if a woman's menstrual bleeding stops after ten days?
A) Immediately upon the cessation of bleeding, even without ghusl.
B) Only after she performs ghusl.
C) After the completion of her habitual cycle, even if it is less than ten days.
D) Never, because ten days is abnormal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school reconciles the two Quranic readings by applying the takhfif reading to cessation after the maximum duration (immediate permissibility) and the tashdid reading to cessation at the habit's end (requiring ghusl or exception).

Menstruating and Postpartum Women: Qada for Fasts but Not Prayers
Ruling that only fasts need to be made up, not prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for menstruating and postpartum women, cite the primary dalil, and explain the rationale of hardship and the intra-Hanafi difference on the basis of qada.

Core Idea
Menstruating women make up fasts, not prayers – hardship lifts the prayer qada.

This lesson addresses a distinctive Hanafi ruling: a woman in menstruation or postpartum bleeding is required to make up (qada) any missed fasts, but she is not required to make up any missed prayers. The proof comes from the practice of the Prophet's wives and is supported by consensus and the principle of removing hardship (haraj). We will also explore the intra-Hanafi reasoning on why qada is obligatory even when the original performance was not required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The passage rules on two acts: fasting and prayer. Determine for each whether qada is wajib or not.
Fasts: wajib to make up; prayers: not wajib.
2
Analyse the primary dalil (hadith)
Examine the hadith of Aisha as narrated by Mu'aadhah. Note the explicit command to make up fasts and the absence of command for prayers.
The hadith is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear.
3
Understand the rationale of hardship (haraj)
The text explains that making up fifty prayers per month would cause severe hardship, so it is exempted by text. Making up ten fasts in a year is not a hardship.
Hardship serves as a legitimate excuse for exemption from qada, just as it exempts from performance.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the basis of qada
Note the difference: the majority (jumhur) hold that qada is obligated by the same cause as ada (e.g., entry of time), while some hold it is obligated by a new command.
The practical result is the same; this is a theoretical difference.
5
Consolidate with consensus and cross-madhhab note
The passage states 'upon this there is consensus' – the ruling itself is universally agreed upon by the four schools, though the reasoning may vary.
No school holds that prayers must be made up by a menstruating woman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وتقضي الحائض والنفساءُ الصَّومَ دونَ الصَّلاةِ) لحديث معاذة بنت عبد الله العدوي، قالت: « سَأَلْتُ عَائِشَةَ ، فَقُلْتُ: مَا بَالُ الْحَائِضِ تَقْضِي الصَّوْمَ وَلَا تَقْضِي الصَّلاةَ؟ فَقَالَتْ: أَحَرُورِيَّةٌ أَنْتِ؟ قُلْتُ: لَسْتُ بِحَرُورِيَّةٍ، وَلَكِنِّي أَسْأَلُ قَالَتْ: كَانَ يُصِيبُنَا ذَلِكَ، فَنُؤْمَرُ بِقَضَاءِ الصَّوْمِ وَلَا نُؤْمَرُ بِقَضَاءِ الصَّلاةِ » . وعليه انعقد الإجماع. ولأن الحرج عذر مسقط للقضاء، كما أنه مسقط للأداء، وفي قضاء خمسين صلاة في كل شهر حرج، وهو ساقط بالنص، ولا حرج في قضاء صوم عشرة أيام في سنة، والقضاء يجب بما يجب به الأداء على قول الجمهور من مشايخنا، فيكفي انعقاد السبب لوجوب القضاء، وإن لم يخاطب بالأداء فلذا تقضي الصوم، وإن لم تكن مخاطبة بأدائه، ولا إشكال على قول بعض مشايخنا بأن القضاء يجب بأمر جديد والحرورية فرقة من الخوارج منسوبة إلى حروراء)، قرية بالكوفة كان بها اجتماعهم والمراد أنها في التعمق في سؤالها كانت خارجية، لأنهم تعمقوا في الدين حتى خرجوا منه.
And the menstruating woman and postpartum woman must make up fasting but not prayer. Due to the hadith of Mu'aadhah bint Abdullah al-Adawiyya who said: 'I asked Aisha, said: Why does the menstruating woman make up fasts but not prayers? She replied: Are you a Haruriyyah? I said: I am not a Haruriyyah, but I am asking. She said: That used to happen to us, and we were commanded to make up fasts but not commanded to make up prayers.' Upon this, there is consensus. And because hardship is an excuse that exempts from qada as it exempts from performing, and there is hardship in making up fifty prayers every month, which is exempted by the text, and there is no hardship in making up ten days of fasting in a year. And qada becomes obligatory by that which necessitates performance according to the majority of our scholars. So the existence of the cause is sufficient for the obligation of qada, even if she was not addressed with performance. Hence she makes up fasting even if she was not addressed with its performance. And there is no problem according to some of our scholars that qada is obligated by a new command. And 'Haruriyyah' is a sect of Khawarij attributed to Harura', a village in Kufa where they assembled. The meaning is that in her depth of questioning, she was like a Kharijite, because they delved deep into religion until they left it.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage states the well-established Hanafi ruling that a woman in menstruation or postpartum bleeding must make up (perform qada for) any fasts she missed during that period, but she does not have to make up any prayers she missed. The proof is the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) as narrated by Mu'aadhah. When asked about this difference, Aisha explained that the practice during the time of the Prophet was exactly that. The text also mentions that there is consensus (ijma') on this ruling. The rationale given is the principle of hardship (haraj): making up fifty prayers (approximate number of prayers in a month) every month would be very difficult, and the texts have exempted women from this. In contrast, making up about ten days of fasting in a year is not a great hardship. The passage also clarifies that even if the woman was not obligated to perform the fasts during menses (because she was exempt), she must still make them up later. The majority of Hanafi scholars hold that the cause for qada is the same as the cause for the original obligation (i.e., the entry of the time), while some others hold that qada is a new command. The reference to 'Haruriyyah' is an aside explaining that Aisha's question was not meant to criticize the questioner but to check if she had Kharijite tendencies of excessive strictness.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā’): Making up a missed obligatory act of worship after its prescribed time.
حرج (ḥaraj): Severe hardship or difficulty that justifies exemption from an obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the menstruating woman not have to make up missed prayers according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because prayers are less important than fasting.
B) Because making up a large number of prayers would cause hardship.
C) Because prayers are invalid if performed in a state of impurity.
D) Because the hadith only mentions fasting.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that menstruating and postpartum women must make up missed fasts but not missed prayers, based on the hadith of Aisha, consensus, and the principle of hardship.
